  • CytR and CRP turn off transcription by binding in a highly co-operative fashion to speciﬁc targets in the promoter regions ( Gerlach et al. , 1991 ; Pedersen et al. , 1991 ; 1992 ; 1995 ; Søgaard-Andersen et al. , 1991 ; Holst et al. , 1992 ) . [9767576]
  • This model also offers a plausible explanation for the recent findings that CytR does not regulate transcription from deoP2 in Icya or Acrp strains , although transcription occurs from the same site in deoP2 in the absence and presence of cAMP-CRP ( L. Sogaard-Andersen et al. . [1962841]
  • Thus , in the presence of both cAMP-CRP and CytR , a nucleoprotein complex is formed that most probably contains cAMP-CRP at each CRP site and CytR bound in the intervening region ( Sogaard-Ander-sen et al. 1991 ) . [1661372]

  • Repression of deoP2 Repression of deoP2 by CytR was only observed in the presence of cAMP ± CRP , in agreement with the in vivo observation that CytR binding requires cAMP ± CRP ( Sùgaard-Andersen et al. , 1990a , b ) . [11574471]

  • Cooperative and Competitive Interactions of CytR -- The initial indication and one functional consequence of these interactions is that while saturation of CRP1 and CRP2 greatly increases the apparent affinity of CytR for its putative operator located between these , saturation by CytR has a much lesser effect on the apparent affinity of CRP for CRP1 and CRP2 ( Table I ) ( 21 ) .   • CytR belongs to the LacI repressor family and exhibits extensive amino acid sequence homology to several other members ( e.g. PurR , LacI and GalR ; Weickert and Adhya , 1992 ) . [9155036]
  • First , CytR is member of the LacI/GalR family of transcription regulators . [20000490]
  • Summary The Escherichia coli CytR regulator belongs to the LacI family of sequence-speciﬁc DNA-binding proteins and prevents CRP-mediated transcription in the CytR regulon . [9466254]
  • Whereas inducer or co-repressor binding to other family members controls a switch between DNA-binding protein and non-DNA-binding protein conformations , cytidine binding to CytR affects only cooperative interactions between CytR and CRP . [10347150]
  • Second , CytR exhibits lower DNA binding specificity than other LacI family members and most other bacterial repressors . [10347150]
  • Like other LacI family members , the basic DNA binding unit of CytR is a homodimer ( 6 ) . [10347150]
  • While regulatory ligand binding to most LacI family proteins is coupled intrinsic DNA-binding affinity , in CytR , cytidine binding is coupled to protein-protein cooperativity and not to intrinsic protein-DNA-binding affinity . [20000490]
  • CytR is unique among LacI/GalR family members in that binding of its regulatory ligand , cytidine , is linked not to DNA-binding affinity but instead to the cooperative interactions between CytR bound at CytO and CRP bound to CRP1 and CRP2 . [20000490]
  • A comparison of the GntR primar structure with those of the repressors in the CytR family revealed that GntR also has a helix-turn-helix motif at its N-terminus , which may be responsible for DNA binding and it may also have domains related to dimerization and inducer binding at its C-terminus ( Weickert & Adhya , 1992 ) . [9135111]
  • The CytR repressor belongs to the LacI family of regulators , and possesses , like the other members , an N-terminal helix -- turn -- helix ( HTH ) DNA-binding motif ( Valentin-Hansen et al. , 1986 ; Weickert and Adhya , 1992 ) . [9155036]
  • CytR is a sequence-specific DNA-binding protein and a member of the LacllGalR family of sequence-specific DNA-binding proteins ( Pedersen et al. , 1991 ; ValentinHansen et al. , 1986 ; for review see Weickert and Adhya , 1992 ) . [8221894]

  • Although CytR binds to an additional site located just downstream from the transcription start site as noted above , there is no interaction between CytR binding to this site and CytR/CRP binding to CRP2 , CytO , and CRP1 . [20000490]

  • The possibilities are 1 ) that the additional CytR sites that overlap CRP1 and CRP2 are specific binding sites to which CytR binds noncooperatively and with defined affinity ; and 2 ) that the additional binding is nonspecific but cooperative . [8969182]
